               <div class="article-section__table-source"></div>
            </div>
            
            <p>Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202401188-fig-0005">5b</a> shows the third reversible sodiation/desodiation of the investigated electrodes with a mass loading of&nbsp;≈0.5 mg&nbsp;cm<sup>−2</sup> at 50&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, after a preconditioning of three cycles at 40&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> was conducted (the sixth total cycle is shown). The reversible specific capacities for each electrode are listed in Table&nbsp;<a class="tableLink scrollableLink" title="Link to table" href="#adfm202401188-tbl-0002">2</a>. Among all the tested MPNC23 electrodes, the MPNC23-1300 and MPNC23-1500 performed best with specific capacities of ≈190&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>.</p>
            
            <p>For the MPNC23-1000 sample, a voltage profile dominated by sloping contributions with an overall low specific capacity of only 146&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> is observed. Due to the abundant presence of heteroatoms in this electrode (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202401188-fig-0002">2k</a>), it is reasonable to assume a significant number of surface functional groups are taking part in sodium uptake, resulting in the observed sloping voltage profile. The other samples show a clear distinction between a sloping region (&gt;100&nbsp;mV&nbsp;vs&nbsp;Na/Na<sup>+</sup>) and a plateau region (&lt;100&nbsp;mV&nbsp;vs&nbsp;Na/Na<sup>+</sup>), as visualized for the MPNC23-1500 sample in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202401188-fig-0006">6a</a>. Their contributions to the overall specific capacity (Table&nbsp;<a class="tableLink scrollableLink" title="Link to table" href="#adfm202401188-tbl-0002">2</a>, Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202401188-fig-0006">6b,c</a>) show a declining sloping capacity with increasing graphitization temperatures, while the plateau capacity increases until a graphitization temperature of 1500&nbsp;°C is reached and only then starts to decrease with higher graphitization temperatures. To further investigate the trend of declining plateau capacities toward higher graphitization temperatures, we also investigated graphite as an anode material with an extremely narrow <i>d</i>-spacing (<i>d</i><sub>002</sub>&nbsp; = &nbsp;3.36 Å), yielding a low overall specific capacity of only 19&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, with only 9 % of the specific capacity in the plateau regime (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adfm202401188-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/ade758c7-b1c6-41e1-9783-743a198ece23/adfm202401188-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/ade758c7-b1c6-41e1-9783-743a198ece23/adfm202401188-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/6e4fcb71-4213-431e-bdcf-c977e00151d6/adfm202401188-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/ade758c7-b1c6-41e1-9783-743a198ece23/adfm202401188-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202401188-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202401188" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Separation of voltage profiles into a sloping (&gt;100&nbsp;mV vs Na/Na<sup>+</sup>) and plateau region (&lt;100&nbsp;mV vs Na/Na+). a)&nbsp;Graphical visualization of the separation between sloping (orange) and plateau (green) capacity, shown for the MPNC23-1500 electrode. b) Representation of the contributions of sloping and plateau capacity for the different graphitization temperatures. c) Contribution of each voltage regime to the overall achieved specific capacity at 50&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>The sloping region is commonly associated with the surface adsorption of sodium ions on defect sites.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0051" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0051_R_d263571606e1648" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 51 - Nano Lett.">51</a>, <a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0053" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0053_R_d263571606e1648" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 53 - Carbon">53</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In line with the combined observations from the conducted elemental analysis, Raman, XRD, and HRTEM measurements (summarized in Figures&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202401188-fig-0002">2</a> and 3), the decline in sloping capacity is rationalized by the observed decline in heteroatoms and an increase in internal ordering. The plateau capacity has been repeatedly linked to the intercalation of sodium ions into the pseudo-graphitic interspace,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0030_R_d263571606e1656" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - ACS Nano">30</a>, <a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0051" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0051_R_d263571606e1656" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 51 - Nano Lett.">51</a>-<a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0054" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0054_R_d263571606e1656" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 54 - Nano Energy">54</a>, <a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0094" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0094_R_d263571606e1656" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 94 - ACS Nano">94</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> representing a faradaic energy storage process occurring within a narrow potential range. As the intercalation of sodium ions is sensitive toward the interlayer <i>d</i><sub>002</sub> spacing of the graphitic domains,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0021_R_d263571606e1665" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - RSC Adv.">21</a>, <a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0095" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0095_R_d263571606e1665" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 95 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">95</a>-<a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0097" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0097_R_d263571606e1665" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 97 - J. Energy Chem.">97</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> the evolution of the plateau capacity for the MPNC samples with increasing graphitization temperatures and the exceptionally low plateau capacity of our additional graphite reference can be rationalized with the observed decrease in <i>d</i><sub>002</sub>&nbsp;spacing. At a temperature of 1500&nbsp;°C, it appears that an optimal <i>d</i><sub>002</sub> spacing of 3.65&nbsp;Å within the MPNC temperature series was realized, being neither too narrow nor too wide for a favorable interaction between the negatively charged carbon scaffold and the positively charged sodium ion. This results in the highest observed plateau capacity of 98&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> for MPNC23-1500. The ideal graphitization temperature for a maximum plateau capacity, however, varies for differently prepared hard carbons, as factors like the chosen precursor can strongly influence relevant parameters like the degree of internal crosslinking, which influences the amount of energy needed for a graphitic restructuration. Ghimbeu et&nbsp;al.,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0054" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0054_R_d263571606e1679" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 54 - Nano Energy">54</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> for example, prepared a hard carbon electrode from cellulose, which showed the highest plateau capacity (216&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) within their temperature series (1000–1600&nbsp;°C) at a graphitization temperature&nbsp;of&nbsp;1600&nbsp;°C with a <i>d</i><sub>002</sub>&nbsp;spacing of 3.72&nbsp;Å. In comparison, the prepared MPNC23 series generally shows a narrower <i>d</i><sub>002</sub> spacing for the same graphitization temperatures, which is most likely due to the preexisting aromatic substructures in the MPNC samples originating from the aniline precursor, compared to the non-aromatic cellulose precursor (comparison summarized in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8</a>, Supporting Information). A large contribution of the plateau capacity is favorable, as it stores sodium ions close to the equilibrium potential of the Na/Na<sup>+</sup> system, which defines the lower potential limit in a SIB. Hence, in a full cell battery, a larger plateau capacity will result in a larger energy and power density. Considering this, the MPNC23-1500 sample with the largest plateau capacity contribution and overall specific capacity was further investigated in more detail.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202401188-sec-0060">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="adfm202401188-sec-0060-title">2.4 Energy Storage Mode of the MPNC23-1500 Anode</h3>
            
            <p>A low voltage plateau close to the Na/Na<sup>+</sup> potential is commonly linked to the faradaic energy storage occurring during sodium ion intercalation or micropore filling in hard carbons<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0055" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0055_R_d263571606e1710" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 55 - Chem. Eng. J.">55</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and is desirable for the attainment of high power and energy densities. To verify a predominantly faradaic energy storage mode for the plateau capacity of the MPNC23-1500 electrode, cyclic voltammetry (CV) experiments were carried out. First, four preconditioning scans at 0.1&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202401188-fig-0007">7a</a>) were carried out. In the initial cycle, a dominant peak at 0.45&nbsp;V versus Na/Na<sup>+</sup> during sodiation is observed, which is explained by the formation of a SEI in the respective potential region, as already observed in the initial cycle during the initial galvanostatic sodiation (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202401188-fig-0005">5a</a>). For the subsequent three cycles at 0.1&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>, no peak is visible at 0.45&nbsp;V versus Na/Na<sup>+</sup> and the CV shapes appear stable, proving the excellent stability of the anode under these conditions. With an increasing scan-rate from 0.1 to 1.5&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>, the sodiation and desodiation peak current increases (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202401188-fig-0007">7b</a>). At scan-rates surpassing 1.2&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>, an increasing fluctuation in the reductive current is observed at ≈0.4&nbsp;V versus Na/Na<sup>+</sup>, indicating the emergence of irreversible processes. As this is occurring in the potential regime associated with the formation of the SEI, we assume similar irreversible surface reactions to be associated with the observed reduction current (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S9</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adfm202401188-fig-0007"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/7c516a24-5b50-4761-be95-60c20f98f308/adfm202401188-fig-0007-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/7c516a24-5b50-4761-be95-60c20f98f308/adfm202401188-fig-0007-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/567b0ab3-0a34-48bc-affa-6a1e2517afe1/adfm202401188-fig-0007-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/7c516a24-5b50-4761-be95-60c20f98f308/adfm202401188-fig-0007-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 7<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202401188-fig-0007&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202401188" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Cyclic voltammetry measurements of the MPNC23-1500 electrode as obtained from a half-cell in a three-electrode setup (counter electrode and reference electrode sodium metal, two cells measured, one exemplary shown). a) Initial four cycles at 0.1&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>. b) Scan-rate dependent cyclic&nbsp;voltammograms from 0.1 to 1.5&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>. c) Logarithmic anodic peak current plotted against the logarithmic scan-rate for the investigation of the energy storage mode.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <div class="paragraph-element">Classically, a power-law relationship is assumed, describing the influence of the scan-rate <i>v</i> on the measured peak current&nbsp;<i>i</i> according to Equations&nbsp;(<a class="equationLink scrollableLink" href="#adfm202401188-disp-0001" title="Link to equation">1</a>) and (<a class="equationLink scrollableLink" href="#adfm202401188-disp-0002" title="Link to equation">2</a>), enabling the determination of the constant parameters <i>a</i> and <i>b</i> by performing a simple linear regression.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0098" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0098_R_d263571606e1788" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 98 - J. Phys. Chem. B">98</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup>
               
               <div class="inline-equation" id="adfm202401188-disp-0001"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                     <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/06b7dfe2-bf89-4842-8a89-07c7ede403b3/adfm202401188-math-0001.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:1616301X:media:adfm202401188:adfm202401188-math-0001" display="block" location="graphic/adfm202401188-math-0001.png">
                        <semantics>
                           <mrow>
                              <mi>i</mi>
                              <mo linebreak="badbreak">=</mo>
                              <mi>a</mi>
                              <mo linebreak="goodbreak">×</mo>
                              <mrow></mrow>
                              <msup>
                                 <mi>v</mi>
                                 <mi>b</mi>
                              </msup>
                           </mrow>
                           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation} i=a\ensuremath{\times{}}{v}^{b} \end{equation}$$</annotation>
                        </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(1)</span></div>
               <div class="inline-equation" id="adfm202401188-disp-0002"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                     <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/185984d6-0bc2-4d6b-afaa-e695574a8308/adfm202401188-math-0002.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:1616301X:media:adfm202401188:adfm202401188-math-0002" display="block" location="graphic/adfm202401188-math-0002.png">
                        <semantics>
                           <mrow>
                              <mi>log</mi>
                              <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
                              <mi>i</mi>
                              <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
                              <mo>=</mo>
                              <mi>b</mi>
                              <mo linebreak="goodbreak">×</mo>
                              <mrow></mrow>
                              <mi>log</mi>
                              <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
                              <mi>v</mi>
                              <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
                              <mo>+</mo>
                              <mi>log</mi>
                              <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
                              <mi>a</mi>
                              <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
                           </mrow>
                           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation} \log (i)=b\ensuremath{\times{}}\log(v)+\log (a) \end{equation}$$</annotation>
                        </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(2)</span></div>
            </div>
            
            <p>This model assumes surface-controlled processes for a <i>b</i> value close to 1, while a <i>b</i> value of 0.5 indicates a diffusion-dominated process. The <i>b</i> value of 0.38 is obtained from the slope of Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202401188-fig-0007">7c</a>, indicating, that at the chosen scan-rates, the energy is predominantly stored through a diffusion-controlled faradaic process in contrast to a surface-controlled capacitive one. While values between 0.5 and 1 indicate a mixture of faradaic and capacitive contributions (at ≈0.6, a faradaic process with some capacitive contributions is assumed, while higher values are often described as a pseudocapacitive behavior), values below 0.5 are typically also considered as diffusion-dominated.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0099" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0099_R_d263571606e1856" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 99 - J. Mater. Chem. A">99</a>, <a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0100" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0100_R_d263571606e1856" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 100 - J. Phys. Chem. C">100</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The discrepancy between the ideal 0.5 and lower values can be explained by deviations from the theoretical model applied. The used Randles–Sevcik equation assumes a flat electrode and a perfect semi-infinite diffusion profile.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0101" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0101_R_d263571606e1862" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 101 - J. Solid State Electrochem.">101</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Both conditions are only approximately true for the anodic current response of the MPNC23-1500 electrode. The faradaic nature of the process investigated here is further supported by the observed voltage profile with its well-developed plateau region (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202401188-fig-0006">6a</a>). For its practical application, this faradaic energy storage process must, however, persist even after many cycles (&gt;&nbsp;1000) and under high current densities (≥1000&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) to be able to supply sufficiently high power and energy densities, all while exhibiting a low self-discharge.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202401188-sec-0070">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="adfm202401188-sec-0070-title">2.5 Cycling Performance and Rate Capability</h3>
            
            <p>In the context of large-scale energy storage systems, the cycling performance at elevated current densities holds significant importance, as it influences the duration until its end-of-life and consequently the battery replacement frequency. We herein demonstrate the excellent electro chemical performance of our MPNC23-1500 anode with a mass loading of 0.64&nbsp;mg&nbsp;cm<sup>−2</sup> (comparable range with most studies in literature and especially the herein mentioned studies) in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202401188-fig-0008">8</a>. After 2000 cycles at 1000&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, a capacity retention of 86 %&nbsp;was achieved during galvanostatic charge–discharge experiments, starting with a capacity of 123&nbsp;mAh g<sup>−1</sup> in the initial cycle after preconditioning (consisting of three cycles at 40&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) and still achieving 106&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> in cycle&nbsp;2000 (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202401188-fig-0008">8a</a>). This represents a loss in specific capacity of only 0.04 % per cycle, underscoring the excellent cycling performance of our prepared MPNC23-1500 anode, with a faradaic energy storage, even at high current densities of 1000&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Almost all other anodes, which achieve a similar cycling performance, store energy in a purely capacitive or pseudocapacitive way.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0027_R_d263571606e1902" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">27</a>, <a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0028_R_d263571606e1902" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - J. Power Sources">28</a>, <a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0059" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0059_R_d263571606e1902" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 59 - J. Mater. Chem. A">59</a>, <a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0061" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0061_R_d263571606e1902" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 61 - Nano Res.">61</a>, <a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0102" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0102_R_d263571606e1902" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 102 - Carbon">102</a>, <a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0105" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0105_R_d263571606e1902" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 105 - Energy Environ Mater.">105</a>, <a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0107" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0107_R_d263571606e1902" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 107 - Nano Res.">107</a>, <a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0109" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0109_R_d263571606e1902" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 109 - Rare Met.">109</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adfm202401188-fig-0008"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/5bf564f1-6899-47bc-ad44-d215fc139f00/adfm202401188-fig-0008-m.jpg"><picture>

Mater. Chem. A">59</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> F,<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0026" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0026_R_d263571606e1961" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Adv. Energy Mater.">26</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> G,<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0060" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0060_R_d263571606e1967" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 60 - Energy Storage Mater.">60</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> H,<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0063" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0063_R_d263571606e1972" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 63 - Chin. Chem. Lett.">63</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> I,<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0027" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0027_R_d263571606e1977" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> J,<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0105" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0105_R_d263571606e1983" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 105 - Energy Environ Mater.">105</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> K,<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0061" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0061_R_d263571606e1988" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 61 - Nano Res.">61</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> L,<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0035" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0035_R_d263571606e1993" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - Energy Fuels">35</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> M,<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0028" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0028_R_d263571606e1999" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - J. Power Sources">28</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> N,<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0029" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0029_R_d263571606e2004" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Adv. Energy Mater.">29</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> O,<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0106" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0106_R_d263571606e2009" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 106 - Adv. Mater.">106</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> P,<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0107" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0107_R_d263571606e2015" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 107 - Nano Res.">107</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Q,<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0108" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0108_R_d263571606e2020" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 108 - Carbon">108</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> R<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0109" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0109_R_d263571606e2025" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 109 - Rare Met.">109</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup>]. The reference value (100 %) of each material was set to be the reversible specific capacity of each electrode obtained for the lowest applied current density, in the case of MPNC23-1500 50&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> was used as the reference value.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>The rate capability of a battery systems governs how much energy can be stored with high efficiency even at high current densities and is hence another essential parameter for the application of a battery in large-scale energy storage systems, particularly in scenarios necessitating short-term peak shaving interventions. To test its suitability, our MPNC23-1500 anode was subjected toward a rate test with increasing current densities ranging from 50 to 10&nbsp;000&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. For the last five cycles, the current density was decreased to 100&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> again to evaluate the irreversible capacity losses during the harsher electrochemical conditions of strongly elevated current densities. Furthermore, after the predetermined voltage limits for sodiation (1.5&nbsp;V&nbsp;vs&nbsp;Na/Na<sup>+</sup>) and desodiation (5&nbsp;mV&nbsp;vs&nbsp;Na/Na<sup>+</sup>) were reached, a constant voltage step (CVS) was applied until the measured current at the working electrode fell below one fifth of the formerly applied current density. This CVS is meant to provide the anode with the opportunity to initiate equilibration, which is hardly possible during the high overpotential caused by the polarization at elevated current densities (&gt;1000 mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>). As this CVS leads to an increase in the obtained specific capacities, we proceed to deduct the specific capacity contributions attributed to this CV step for the following discussion (as the CVS contribution is negligible at low current densities, it was not considered for the previous analysis within this work). The usage of such constant voltage steps and their contributions to the overall achieved capacities are unfortunately often not mentioned or discussed in the literature, making comparisons less reliable and less accurate.</p>
            
            <p>Remarkably, the MPNC23-1500 anode achieved a capacity retention of 78 % while the current density is increased from 50 to 1000&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, achieving specific capacities of 162 and 128 mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202401188-fig-0008">8b</a>). Even at extremely high current densities of 10&nbsp;000 mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> a capacity retention of 31 % is observed. While the MPNC23-1500 anode achieved 160&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> during the first five cycles at 100&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, it retained 98.3 % of its specific capacity by achieving 156&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 100&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at the end of the rate test, indicating excellent reversibility and stability even after a harsher electrochemical treatment. As expected, the contribution from the CVS (light pink in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202401188-fig-0008">8b</a>) increases at elevated current densities, as the equilibrium conditions are more difficult to achieve with increasing polarization effects caused by the high current densities. It is reasonable to assume, however, that the overall low mass loading (0.64&nbsp;mg&nbsp;cm<sup>−2</sup>) of the thin MPNC23-1500 anodes keeps the CVS contribution generally small (only 12% even at 10&nbsp;000&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>).</p>
            
            <p>Most reported highly rate capable anodes from literature do not exceed mass loadings of 1.5&nbsp;mg&nbsp;cm,<sup>−2[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0025_R_d263571606e2077" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - J. Mater. Chem. A">25</a>, <a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0029_R_d263571606e2077" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Adv. Energy Mater.">29</a>, <a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0060" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0060_R_d263571606e2077" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 60 - Energy Storage Mater.">60</a>, <a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0061" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0061_R_d263571606e2077" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 61 - Nano Res.">61</a>, <a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0063" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0063_R_d263571606e2077" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 63 - Chin. Chem. Lett.">63</a>, <a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0104" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0104_R_d263571606e2077" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 104 - Electrochim. Acta">104</a>, <a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0108" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0108_R_d263571606e2077" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 108 - Carbon">108</a>, <a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0109" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0109_R_d263571606e2077" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 109 - Rare Met.">109</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> even though a high mass loading is important for practical applications, as it increases the ratio of the active material to inactive material like the current collector and separators, thereby increasing the achievable energy and power density of a complete battery system. We therefore investigated MPNC23-1500 anodes with a more than fourfold higher areal mass loading of 2.7&nbsp;mg&nbsp;cm<sup>−2</sup>, which show a noteworthy capacity retention of 66 % (132 mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) at 1000&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202401188-fig-0008">8c</a>). At 10&nbsp;000&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the electrode only stores energy during the CVS, which is expected, as thicker electrodes tend to possess higher internal resistance and encounter significantly pronounced polarization due to ion diffusion becoming more constrained within the dense electrode matrix.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0107" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0107_R_d263571606e2094" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 107 - Nano Res.">107</a>, <a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0110" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0110_R_d263571606e2094" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 110 - Electrochim. Acta">110</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
            
            <p>In Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202401188-fig-0008">8d</a>, a comparison of the rate capability with the best-performing anode materials we found in literature is presented. All these materials are exclusively or predominantly storing energy in a capacitive storage mode, while our material stores the energy predominantly in a faradaic (diffusion controlled) way (compare Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202401188-fig-0007">7c</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information as well as Equations&nbsp;(<a class="equationLink scrollableLink" href="#adfm202401188-disp-0001" title="Link to equation">1</a>) and (<a class="equationLink scrollableLink" href="#adfm202401188-disp-0002" title="Link to equation">2</a>). The only exceptions are the low rate capability references L and E, which store energy in a mostly faradaic way. All materials, that achieve a higher capacity retention than the MPNC23-1500 anodes, work purely capacitively or pseudocapacitively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0027_R_d263571606e2118" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">27</a>, <a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0029_R_d263571606e2118" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Adv. Energy Mater.">29</a>, <a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0061" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0061_R_d263571606e2118" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 61 - Nano Res.">61</a>, <a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0063" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0063_R_d263571606e2118" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 63 - Chin. Chem. Lett.">63</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This, however, constrains these kinds of anodes from long-term energy storage over hours or days and from achieving higher energy and power densities, which can be ideally visualized by considering the materials in a simulated full cell.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202401188-sec-0080">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="adfm202401188-sec-0080-title">2.6 Theoretical Considerations for Anode Integration in a Full Cell</h3>
            
            <p>In contrast to a linear voltage profile found for capacitive energy storage,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0106" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0106_R_d263571606e2132" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 106 - Adv. Mater.">106</a>-<a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0109" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0109_R_d263571606e2132" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 109 - Rare Met.">109</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> a voltage profile with a plateau region close to the potential of the Na/Na<sup>+</sup> reference system is beneficial for the achievable energy and power density in a full cell, as well as the ability to store electrical energy on a timescale of days or weeks. This is illustrated by a simulated full cell, as schematically shown in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202401188-fig-0009">9a</a>. This simplified model of a charged full cell consists of the fully sodiated anode (experimental data, dark red) and a desodiated cathode with a constant potential of 3.0&nbsp;V&nbsp;versus&nbsp;Na/Na<sup>+</sup> during its sodiation (calculated, blue), being reasonably close to the measured potentials found for Prussian&nbsp;blue<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0015_R_d263571606e2148" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - J. Am. Chem. Soc.">15</a>, <a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0016_R_d263571606e2148" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Chem. Commun.">16</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and polyanion<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0017_R_d263571606e2153" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - J. Mater. Chem.">17</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> based cathode materials. Taking the voltage difference between the anode and the cathode (light red), the energy density within this simulated full cell is readily obtained by integrating the voltage difference with respect to the specific capacity, while the power density of a full cell is the product of the average charge/discharge voltage (dark yellow) and the applied current density (1000&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>).</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adfm202401188-fig-0009"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/995a8291-94b9-4914-97e4-0d827be07a85/adfm202401188-fig-0009-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/995a8291-94b9-4914-97e4-0d827be07a85/adfm202401188-fig-0009-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/dc4cdeeb-455a-4c86-8ab4-fbd40c8e4cf6/adfm202401188-fig-0009-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/995a8291-94b9-4914-97e4-0d827be07a85/adfm202401188-fig-0009-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 9<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202401188-fig-0009&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202401188" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Simulated integration of the prepared MPNC23-1500 anode into a full cell with a simulated cathode with a constant voltage of 3.0&nbsp;V&nbsp;versus&nbsp;Na/Na<sup>+</sup>. a) Schematic illustration of the Na/Na<sup>+</sup> potential (black), the simulated cathode potential (blue), the MPNC23-1500 desodiation profile (dark red) and its corresponding average voltage (orange), the calculated voltage profile of the resulting simulated full cell (light red) and its corresponding average full cell discharge voltage (dark yellow). b) Power density for specific current densities and c) Ragone plot comparing the MPNC23-1500 anode (counter electrode and reference electrode sodium metal, three electrodes measured) with highly rate capable half-cell setups from literature, which were also paired with the simulated cathode with a constant voltage of 3.0&nbsp;V&nbsp;versus&nbsp;Na/Na<sup>+</sup> [O,<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0106" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0106_R_d263571606e2186" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 106 - Adv. Mater.">106</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> P,<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0107" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0107_R_d263571606e2192" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 107 - Nano Res.">107</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Q,<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0108" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0108_R_d263571606e2197" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 108 - Carbon">108</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> R<sup>[</sup><span class="figureLink bibLink tab-link"><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0109" class="figureLink bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0109_R_d263571606e2202" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 109 - Rare Met.">109</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup>]. c) Current density dependent voltage profile of the simulated full cell utilizing the MPNC23-1500 anode.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>The relationship between the achievable energy and power density is commonly displayed in a Ragone diagram (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202401188-fig-0009">9c</a>), showing the outstanding performance of the MPNC23-1500 anode (mass loading&nbsp;=&nbsp;0.64&nbsp;mg&nbsp;cm<sup>−2</sup>) within the simulated full cell. The calculated power densities from four reference high-performance SIB anode materials achieve 1280<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0106" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0106_R_d263571606e2215" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 106 - Adv. Mater.">106</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> 2000<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0107" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0107_R_d263571606e2220" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 107 - Nano Res.">107</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> 1840<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0108" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0108_R_d263571606e2226" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 108 - Carbon">108</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> 1830&nbsp;W&nbsp;kg<sup>−1[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0109" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0109_R_d263571606e2231" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 109 - Rare Met.">109</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> at 1000&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, while the MPNC23-1500 anode prepared herein outperforms these values by 33 % to 200 % with a calculated power density of 2680&nbsp;W&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> at 1000&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202401188-fig-0009">9b</a>, average voltage of 2.68&nbsp;V&nbsp;vs&nbsp;Na/Na<sup>+</sup> multiplied with 1000&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>). This remarkable performance is reasoned by the well-developed voltage plateau even under higher current densities (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202401188-fig-0009">9d</a>). Within the simulated full cell, the MPNC23-1500 anodes achieve calculated desodiation voltages of 2.7&nbsp;V&nbsp;versus&nbsp;Na/Na<sup>+</sup>&nbsp;−2.6&nbsp;V&nbsp;versus&nbsp;Na/Na<sup>+</sup> in the range of 50&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>&nbsp;–&nbsp;5000&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, while still achieving 2.3&nbsp;V&nbsp;versus Na/Na<sup>+</sup> at the highest applied current density of 10&nbsp;000&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (compared to an average desodiation potential of 1.5&nbsp;V&nbsp;vs&nbsp;Na/Na<sup>+</sup> for purely capacitive voltage profiles at all current densities). This translates into remarkably high theoretical power densities of 270, 1350, 2680, and 23&nbsp;300&nbsp;W&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> at 100, 500, 1000, and 10&nbsp;000&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202401188-fig-0009">9b</a>).</p>
            
            <p>The well-developed voltage plateau of the MPNC23-1500 further contributes to achieving high theoretical energy densities of 420, 380, 340, and 114&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup>at 100, 500, 1000, and 10&nbsp;000&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. These values put the MPNC23-1500 electrode within the superior category in relation to the previously consulted literature references. For instance, at 1000&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> the literature anodes achieve energy densities of 385<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0106" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0106_R_d263571606e2285" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 106 - Adv. Mater.">106</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> 163,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0107" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0107_R_d263571606e2291" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 107 - Nano Res.">107</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> 150,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0108" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0108_R_d263571606e2296" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 108 - Carbon">108</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and 394&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg,<sup>−1[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0109" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0109_R_d263571606e2301" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 109 - Rare Met.">109</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> while the MPNC23-1500 anode achieves 340&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup>.</p>
            
            <p>We assume three major properties of the MPNC23-1500 anode to be beneficial for its excellent rate capability and stable plateau capacity, even under high current densities. First, a large surface area (BET-surface&nbsp;area of MPNC23-1500&nbsp;=&nbsp;296&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) increases the electrolyte-electrode interface at which the sodium ions are either adsorbed or channeled into the carbon matrix via charge transfer. A large surface area thereby facilitates sodium uptake. Second, the spherical shape of the particles is assumed to be beneficial for an isotropic electron transport, as their high theoretical packing density lowers the contact resistance between the particles in all three spatial dimensions. Furthermore, the packing of the nanospheres is assumed to lower the tortuosity, thereby enhancing ion diffusion in the interparticular space. Third, the mesoporous structure of the MPNC lowers the average diffusion path length in the solid carbon matrix, as the high porosity exposes the otherwise more difficult-to-access interior of the electrode. While the sodium ion diffusion processes within the electrode are highly complex and not fully understood yet, it could be reasonable to assume that this severely influences the rate capability, considering that the diffusion coefficient of the sodium ion in the chosen 1&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span>&nbsp;NaPF<sub>6</sub> in EC/DEC (50:50&nbsp;wt. %) electrolyte is around five orders of magnitude larger than that of sodium in a hard carbon matrix (3·10<sup>−6</sup>&nbsp;cm<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> in the electrolyte<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0111" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0111_R_d263571606e2327" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 111 - J. Electrochem. Soc.">111</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> vs 2.50·10<sup>−11</sup>&nbsp;cm<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> in a hard carbon matrix).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0112" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0112_R_d263571606e2339" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 112 - ACS Phys. Chem. Au">112</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup>` Sodium ion intercalation, which is associated with the well-developed voltage plateau responsible for the high power densities in the MPNC23-1500 electrode, could strongly benefit from this accessibility, as it would otherwise be reliant on the strongly hindered diffusion through the carbon matrix.</p>
            </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202401188-sec-0090">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202401188-sec-0090-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In conclusion, mesoporous N-doped carbon nanospheres (MPNC) have been successfully synthesized by a silica-based hard templating approach combined with the oxidative polymerization of aniline, yielding a narrow particle size distribution (≈289&nbsp;nm for 1000&nbsp;°C graphitization and 249&nbsp;nm for 2000&nbsp;°C graphitization) and a narrow pore size distribution (20–35&nbsp;nm), enabling the investigation of the ideal graphitization temperature between 1000 and 2000 °C for sodium ion storage in the faradaic plateau region, while keeping the particle morphology and pore size distribution mainly constant. A graphitization temperature of 1500&nbsp;°C, corresponding to a <i>d</i><sub>002</sub> spacing of 3.65&nbsp;Å yields the best results, achieving a specific capacity of 192&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 50 mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, of which 98 mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> originate from the plateau region (&lt;100&nbsp;mV&nbsp;vs&nbsp;Na/Na<sup>+</sup>) and 93 mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> originate from the sloping region (&gt;100&nbsp;mV&nbsp;vs&nbsp;Na/Na<sup>+</sup>). The excellent stability of our MPNC23-1500-anode was proven after 2000 cycles at an elevated current density of 1000&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, only losing 0.04 % of its specific capacity per cycle. We assume that the unique microstructure of the MPNC23-1500 offers a large electrode/electrolyte interface, short solid diffusion pathways for sodium ions and low tortuosity in the interparticular space within the electrode. The capacity retention, when the current density is increased 20-fold from 50 to 1000&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> was 78 % and at current densities of 10&nbsp;000 mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> a capacity retention of 31 % was observed. This capacity retention, in contrast to earlier approaches in literature, was achieved while maintaining a significant faradaic contribution to the stored energy visible as a low voltage plateau during desodiation. This results in very high-power densities in a simulated full cell setup of 2680&nbsp;W&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> at a desodiation current density of 1000&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, while achieving a total specific energy of 340&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup>, marking an increase in power density of at least 33 % compared to the most competitive values we could find in literature for this current density. Owing to these compelling results, we consider this to be a very promising step toward the development of an improved SIB anode material, with an optimized graphitization degree i.e. microstructure for high-power applications as required in grid-scale energy storage systems.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202401188-sec-0100">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202401188-sec-0100-title">4 Experimental Section</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202401188-sec-0110">
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202401188-sec-0120">
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202401188-sec-0130">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202401188-sec-0130-title"> Synthesis of Mesoporous N-Doped Carbon Nanospheres with 23&nbsp;nm Pores</h4>
                  
                  <p>MPNCs were synthesized via an ammoniumpersulfate (APS)-triggered oxidative polymerization of aniline in the presence of silica nanoparticles as the hard template, as reported similarly in previous studies.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0074" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0074_R_d263571606e2401" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 74 - Carbon">74</a>-<a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0077" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0077_R_d263571606e2401" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 77 - Small">77</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Briefly, 1&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span> HCl (Fisher Scientific, prepared by dilution of 5&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span> HCl with MilliQ-water) was added to Milli-Q water, followed by the addition of SiO<sub>2</sub> nanoparticles (Ludox TMA, Sigma–Aldrich, 23&nbsp;nm, 34&nbsp;wt. % in H2O) and aniline (Sigma–Aldrich, ≥99.5 %) as the carbon and nitrogen precursor. Second, a clear solution of APS (Sigma Aldrich, ≥98 %) in HCl (1&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span>) was added dropwise at a constant rate for ≈30&nbsp;min. The mixture was vigorously stirred under air and constant cooling to 0&nbsp;°C for ≈6 h, until the mixture was left to warm up. The stirring was stopped after 24&nbsp;h. The thus obtained dark green solution was washed with Milli-Q water until a conductivity of 0.3&nbsp;mS was measured. A dark powder was obtained after the washed solution was subjected to freeze drying (Alpha 3–4 LSCbasic, Christ) and was subsequently carbonized in a tube furnace (Carbolite Gero GmbH &amp; Co. KG) at 1000&nbsp;°C (200&nbsp;°C h<sup>−1</sup>) for 6&nbsp;h under constant nitrogen flow (150&nbsp;mL min<sup>−1</sup>). Removal of the silica template was accomplished by stirring the composite in a 4&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span> ammonium hydrogen bifluoride solution (NH<sub>4</sub>HF<sub>2</sub>, ≥98 %, Carl Roth GmbH) for 20&nbsp;h. A black powder was obtained after filtration and subsequent drying (60&nbsp;°C). This powder was then subjected to a post-synthesis heat treatment in a tube furnace at 500&nbsp;°C for 2&nbsp;h under constant nitrogen flow (150&nbsp;mL&nbsp;min<sup>−1</sup>). The sample obtained herein was marked MPNC23-1000 (Batch A). For the temperature study, this sample was subjected to 1300&nbsp;°C (150&nbsp;mL min<sup>−1</sup> nitrogen, 3&nbsp;h hold) and 1700&nbsp;°C (33&nbsp;mL&nbsp;min<sup>−1</sup> argon, 3&nbsp;h hold), yielding the samples MPNC23-1300 and MPNC23-1700. The MPNC23-1500 (Batch B) and MPNC23-2000 (Batch C) samples were prepared analogously at their respective temperatures.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202401188-sec-0140">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202401188-sec-0140-title"> Characterization</h4>
                  
                  <p>The sample morphology was assessed by SEM (SU8220, Hitachi&nbsp;High-Technologies Corp.) at acceleration voltages in the range of 2–5&nbsp;kV. The HRTEM and SAED data were collected using the FEI Talos F200X instrument, operated at 200&nbsp;kV. The conversion of the SAED data to simulated PXRD was performed using ImageJ software and EDP2XRD package.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202401188-bib-0113" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202401188-bib-0113_R_d263571606e2441" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 113 - J. Appl. Crystallogr.">113</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The morphology was investigated by N<sub>2</sub> physisorption (3&nbsp;P&nbsp;Micro&nbsp;300, 3P Instruments GmbH&nbsp;&amp;&nbsp;Co. KG) at 77.35&nbsp;K. The particles size distributions were obtained using a quenched solid state density functional theory model of the Quantochrome AsiQwin software in the assumption of slit, cylindrical and spherical pores. The elemental composition was obtained by elemental analysis (MICRO cube, Elementar&nbsp;Analysensysteme&nbsp;GmbH), while the structure of the MPNC samples was further analyzed using a copper anode (λ&nbsp; = &nbsp;1.541 874 Å)&nbsp;XRD (Discover&nbsp;D8, Bruker&nbsp;Corp.) in Bragg-Brentano geometry. Raman measurements were realized using a Raman microscope (Senterra&nbsp;II,&nbsp;Bruker&nbsp;Corp.) with a laser wavelength of 532&nbsp;nm at a power output between 0.25&nbsp;mW and 2.5&nbsp;mW.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202401188-sec-0150">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202401188-sec-0150-title"> Electrochemical Measurements</h4>
                  
                  <p>All electrochemical tests were performed in T-type Swagelock half-cells. The working electrode was prepared by mixing the MPNC23 active material with carbon black (Super C65 Cond., Nanografi) as a conductive agent, carboxymethyl cellulose (≥99.5 %, MSE Supplies) and styrene-butadiene rubber (≥99.5&nbsp;%, MSE Supplies) as a binder in a weight ratio of 80:10:5:5, in water, respectively. As a reference, graphite (&gt;99&nbsp;%, MSE Supplies) anodes were prepared as well. The given mass loading only refers to the active material (e.g.,&nbsp;MPNC23). A highly dispersed ink was obtained by tip-sonication (Sonifier SFX150, Branson, 30&nbsp;min total sonication time, 2&nbsp;s pulses, 60&nbsp;% power) and was then spray coated on an aluminum substrate heated to 100&nbsp;°C. The resulting electrode sheet was then dried in a vacuum drying oven at 60&nbsp;°C. Electrode discs with a diameter of 12&nbsp;mm&nbsp;were obtained using an EL-cut punch (EL-Cell). The final mass loading of the electrodes was found to be between 0.5 and 0.7&nbsp;mg&nbsp;cm<sup>−2</sup>. The T-cells were assembled inside an argon-filled glovebox (MBRAUN, &lt;0.5&nbsp;ppm H<sub>2</sub>O, &lt;0.1&nbsp;ppm&nbsp;O<sub>2</sub>). Sodium chips (≥99.7&nbsp;%, YUNJI Ener. sol., 14&nbsp;mm diameter) were used, from which the 12&nbsp;mm counter electrodes were punched out. The sodium leftovers were used for the reference electrode. The battery compartments were separated by 13 and 10&nbsp;mm binder-free glass microfibers (Whatman, GF/C). Separators between the counter and the working electrode were soaked with 80&nbsp;µl of the 1&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span> NaPF<sub>6</sub>&nbsp;electrolyte (in ethylencarbonate/diethylcarbonate, 50:50&nbsp;wt. %., E-Lyte Innov.), while the separators of the reference electrode were soaked with 40&nbsp;µl of the same electrolyte. Electrochemical measurements were performed using Biologic potentiostats at room temperature. For all charge/discharge experiments, after the sodiation (1.5&nbsp;V&nbsp;vs&nbsp;Na/Na<sup>+</sup>) and desodiation voltage limits (5&nbsp;mV&nbsp;vs&nbsp;Na/Na<sup>+</sup>) were reached, a constant voltage step (CVS) at the respective limit was applied until the measured current fell below one fifth of the originally applied current density, giving the system additional time to equilibrate.</p>
                  </section>
               </section>
            </section>
         </section>

                  <li data-bib-id="adfm202401188-bib-0001"><span class="bullet">1</span><span class="author">M. A. Hannan</span>, <span class="author">S. B. Wali</span>, <span class="author">P. J.
